<div class=\"widget widget-ArticleFulltext widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=129345898 id=\"129345898\" class=\"abstract-title\" >ABSTRACT</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Gravitationally lensed quasars are valuable, but extremely rare, probes of observational cosmology and extragalactic astrophysics. Progress in these fields has been limited just by the paucity of systems with good ancillary data. Here we present a first spectroscopic confirmation of lenses discovered in the Southern Sky from the DES and KiDS-DR3 footprints. We have targeted seven high-graded candidates, selected with new techniques, with NTT-EFOSC2, and confirmed five of them. We provide source spectroscopic redshifts, image separations, <em>gri</em> photometry, and first lens model parameters. The success rate of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\sim } 70{{\\ \\rm per\\ cent}}$|</span> confirms our forecasts, based on the comparison between the number of candidate doubles and quadruplets in our searches over a \u22485000\u00a0deg<sup>2</sup> footprint and theoretical predictions.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"surveys\">surveys</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;Galaxies: formation&quot;\">Galaxies: formation</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=129345900 id=\"129345900\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">When a quasar (QSO) is strongly lensed by a galaxy, it results in multiple images of the same source, possibly accompanied by arcs or rings that map the lensed host galaxy. The light curves of different images are offset by a measurable time delay that depends on cosmological distances to lens and source and the gravitational potential of the lens (Refsdal <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1964</a>), which in turn enables one-step measurements of the expansion history of the Universe and the dark-matter haloes of massive lens galaxies at up to <em>z</em> \u223c 0.5 (e.g. Suyu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). The microlensing effect on the multiple QSO images, induced by stars in the deflector, provides a quantitative handle on the stellar content of the lens galaxies (e.g. Schechter\u00a0&amp; Wambsganss <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Bate et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Oguri, Rusu\u00a0&amp; Falco <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>) and, simultaneously, can constrain the inner structure of the source quasar, both accretion disc size and thermal profile (e.g. Anguita et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Eigenbrod et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Motta et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) as well as the geometry of the broad-line region (e.g. Sluse et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Guerras et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Braibant et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). Finally, source reconstruction of the lensed QSO and its host give a direct view of QSO-host co-evolution up to <em>z</em> \u223c 2 (e.g. Peng et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Ding et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). However, lensed quasars are rare on the sky: typically \u223c0.1 per deg<sup>2</sup> at depth and resolution of present-day surveys (Oguri\u00a0&amp; Marshall <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>, hereafter <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">OM10</a>), since they require a very close alignment of quasars with foreground massive galaxies, or galaxy clusters. The advent of various wide-field surveys, charting extended areas in both hemispheres, helps to overcome the intrinsic rarity of lensed quasars, provided that suitable techniques are devised in order to mine them in massive data bases.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Within our team, we have developed multiple techniques of data mining for lensed quasar searches and recently applied them with success to the Kilo Degree Survey and to the Dark Energy Survey (Agnello\u00a0&amp; Spiniello <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a> and Spiniello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>, hereafter <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> and\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">S18</a>, respectively). We combined different methods to pre-select QSOs, tested their performance and complementarity, and published a list of high-grade candidates, to facilitate (possibly independent) spectroscopic follow-up campaigns.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Here, we present results from the first of these follow-up campaigns, based on data acquired with EFOSC2 (the ESO Faint Object Spectrograph and Camera) mounted at the Nasmyth B focus of the 3.6\u00a0m New Technology Telescope (NTT). We give details of the selected candidates in the next section (Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a>). We report on the spectroscopic run in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a> and provide photometry and lens model results in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>. We finally conclude in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>. Whenever needed, we adopt a flat lambda cold dark matter cosmology with \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>\u00a0= 0.7 and <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0= 70\u2009km\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup>\u00a0Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>. Magnitudes from DES and KiDS are in the AB system while the ones from WISE are in the Vega system.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=129345904 id=\"129345904\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 CANDIDATE SELECTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We selected our candidates from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">S18</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>, and from a more recent (hitherto unpublished) list of high-grade candidates found in a similar way. We refer to the two mentioned papers for a detailed description of the morphology- and photometry-based methods that we developed to find lens candidates in wide-sky photometric multiband surveys. The new DES candidates were selected using astrometric offsets of WISE-preselected objects (with the same WISE cuts as in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>) between DES and <em>Gaia</em> J2000 coordinates, whereas in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> we were considering offsets between 2MASS and <em>Gaia</em> coordinates. The reason behind this method can be explained by noting that if the deflector and quasar images contribute differently in different bands or in data with different image quality, this should result in centroid offsets of the same object among different surveys. We followed the same procedure as in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> to detrend such astrometric offsets, and targets were required to have field-corrected offsets between 0.27 and 2.0\u00a0arcsec (following tests by <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">S18</a> and\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Targets were then visually inspected via the NCSA-DES access cut-out server<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn1\" data-open=\"fn1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">1</a></sup> to assemble a final list of candidates. Some high-grade candidates were lost at visual inspection, due to visualization issues from large queries in the NCSA web interface (we expected this since <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>). As per STRIDES<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn2\" data-open=\"fn2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">2</a></sup> internal agreements, the full list of lens candidates from DES-versus-<em>Gaia</em> offsets will not be disclosed yet.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Some of our candidates have also been found by another group at the same time (Lemon et\u00a0al. in preparation). Following publication agreements within STRIDES, we give here partially blinded coordinates for two of them. Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> reports coordinates and infrared magnitudes (used in the stage of pre-selection) of the systems.</p>                        <a id=\"129345908\" scrollto-destination=\"129345908\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl1\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table 1.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">List of observed candidates with the infrared magnitudes from the WISE catalogue (Wright et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) that have been used at the pre-selection stage (for some systems, errors of magnitudes are missing from the WISE catalogue). paper, and L18\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/129345908\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">For all the candidates, we perform Direct Image Analysis (DIA), as detailed in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">S18</a>. Briefly, a PSF model is fit and subsequently subtracted from the survey image to check for the presence of signal from the deflector. In particular, using the <span class=\"small-caps\">pyraf</span> package<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn3\" data-open=\"fn3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">3</a></sup> on the <em>r</em>-band images, we simultaneously fit a point-PSF model to the QSO multiple images. We then generated subtracted images which we visually inspect to identify the position of the deflector. For the DES systems, DIA was performed after the spectroscopic run, since we did not use it in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We show the <em>gri</em> cut-outs (left-hand panel) and the DIA residuals (right-hand panels) for the candidates reported in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> and\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">S18</a> in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>, and for the new candidates presented in this paper in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>.</p> data-section=\"129345912\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/483/3/10.1093_mnras_sty3407/1/sty3407fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611465312&Signature=HLSC9bhBh8fQ1rwuLSlWGJTEpC5IGZz31sZ4yDhVHJ7yVfVdfjiNABNIOhyZiu0XpOUsqbFJ1y3yu3iHrd5dduVo6VbFs9yz3uQzmr0oxRdsGaDfbOM2DEPVXr8ujPTefoWIj8hfRSg8F6SLx0YQRtK-2fNfoNWD8~zotHToqVUjyy4Qd9LxMxvDCNKtWvUotPZe0NCz0Y7lH0rJQ0iL2H9CAFfuN5J0UARsf-S3hABb6oiN-v5ReCyHgM0MFoMUAsiCgdcAVTKoJI99HGAMhek5uEpDnq2QH4dMuqCNwcbAk7F0Y2FlztTk~h7V6RR3HysLkPK20joCOp~J-CXlzg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=129345912&ar=5251843&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" as in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>) for the new candidates presented in this paper.</p></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=129345913 id=\"129345913\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 SPECTROSCOPIC FOLLOW-UP</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Three nights on NTT-EFOSC2 (P0101.A-0298, PI: Anguita) were allocated for follow-up in 2018 July. However, the run was mostly weathered out and we could observe only seven candidates, each with 20 min of integration time. The seeing was stable at 1.0 \u00b1 0.2\u00a0arcsec, spectra were reduced using standard (ESO-released) pipelines, and the quasar traces were optimally de-blended using a superpostion of Gaussian profiles in the spatial direction (see Morgan et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>; Agnello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We have confirmed five out of seven lenses, selected from wide-sky photometric surveys, namely DES and KiDS, in the Southern Sky. Concerning the two remaining candidates, KIDS2300-3104 resulted to be a couple of stars, while for bf DES2105-4249 only one trace showed emission lines in its spectrum. This system is therefore not a lensed quasar where the two point-like sources are multiple images of the same object. It is most likely a projection effect of a galaxy\u00a0+\u00a0QSOs.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This success rate of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\sim }70{{\\ \\rm per\\ cent}}$|</span> is slightly higher but still consistent with the estimates from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>, considering the number of high-graded candidates versus the number of expected lenses over the DES footprint (adopting the lensing rates by <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">OM10</a>).</p><div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">The NTT spectra of the five confirmed lensed QSOs are shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>, where we also highlight some of the stronger emission lines that enabled the determination of source redshifts, such as CIV\u00a0\u03bb1549, L\u03b1, or Mg\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>\u00a0\u03bb2799. The redshifts were determined with a simultaneous Gaussian fitting to the main emission lines on the spectra of the single components of the quasars, after subtracting the continuum with a fourth-order polynomial function. We note that, although some features deviate from a Gaussian profile, this assumption is sufficient to correctly fit the peak of the lines and measure the redshift of their central wavelength. Once identified the <em>i</em>-th emission lines and their rest-frame wavelength (<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">\u2060|$\\lambda _{0, \\rm i}$|\u2060</span>), we defined the peaks of the Gaussians as <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\lambda _{0, \\rm i}(1+z)$|\u2060</span>, hence <em><em>z</em></em> is a common free parameter for the fitting function, defined as <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"update2011118_update2011118_equ1\" content-id=\"update2011118_update2011118_equ1\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray*}\r\n\\Sigma _{i} A_i \\mathrm{ e}^\\frac{[(\\lambda -\\lambda _{0, \\rm i})(1+z)]^2}{2\\sigma _i^2}, \r\n\\end{eqnarray*} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(1)</span></div>where <em>A<sub>i</sub></em> are normalization factors which account for the peak high, and \u03c3<sub><em>i</em></sub> measure the width of the line. In order to assess the statistical error on the redshift estimates, we have resampled 100\u00a0times the spectrum of every source in the fitted range including the three brightest emission-line features. We have randomly re-extracted each pixel value around the current one assuming Gaussian noise given by the rms of the continuum in the regions close to the fitting window. We have then obtained the mean and standard deviation of the best-fitting redshift obtained using a Levenberg\u2013Marquardt method for \u03c7<sup>2</sup> minimization over the 100 resampled spectra. These are reported in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> for all confirmed quasars as final redshift estimates with their statistical uncertainty.</div>                        <a id=\"129345918\" scrollto-destination=\"129345918\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/483/3/10.1093_mnras_sty3407/1/m_sty3407fig3.jpeg?Expires=1611465313&amp;Signature=mVQC07LIPVHGiFvOXfKsEVoHBHI9xWRjzvb9ALyHETgSKqKGhSYs5R3Sm9xNCZa1gxrZrc9qIlF26pF4psZfj1TG6oXy-4XcACYGtba3ykykFiOzn7-qn4U~IbrIhVW0qsmkjN4RSb4aMd-6Uow-gz1ZNF5jnRpKrKZEFnbR1HiwkkzzMZWMaxjVn1oDU9PKAYit6AgjMLCCmFWf3JTCuCjOkxp~XmwOV2ENi-E1GKcTvKz8N2Fmd92afQkWA~5fr98e-Ayy-HRLQFbJC2hl6j2zqqMWRAfPWhKfj6GAr3xIjq~eZ4-brCN0l8xJ4Y2GDuxVkEe7xyM0~PMbM~X15g__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"1D extracted spectra of the two quasar images for the five confirmed new lenses. The wavelength is always plotted in the observed frame.\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig3.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/129345918/sty3407fig3.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig3.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"129345918\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/483/3/10.1093_mnras_sty3407/1/sty3407fig3.jpeg?Expires=1611465313&Signature=juyoOOPc-4JdY0sUKI-x6lefjBq51N91MIZyB4PN2Yl-fBICAN7uoB4Gs6WqxY~TgehCgWv7sPGSQmdIgs2E9UzTk~KJIXjh0GDurdoo2oGBlc50y1r41A1j0Om8V9TNupWJl53isw4NEpXh72nnzyRgRSmNCBjXzIxOUjxMSIy4hHM~FeHUTQYc6dzsKV4rVRYIZLCYKVZBzTI1-VQLipYq7NYD5bRj0RB22e3Q1OCx3xIcyGMBi38S-IBRQ1b5c3YHtvkxfDO0V0L-TNGBd5zDr3nhAqEhX1Ib3uSYWFmFvOacxGkQ8vCeavtWQFYzOvas2nb9dEbdwBfl8jvDpw__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=129345918&ar=5251843&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig3.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">1D extracted spectra of the two quasar images for the five confirmed new lenses. class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/129345919\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Unfortunately, the faint traces of the lensing galaxies in the spectra did not allow us to securely identify deflector redshifts using the same method. We then estimate photometric redshift distributions using deflector magnitudes from the DES and KIDS multiband images, as explained below.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Using <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> (Peng et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>) we performed PSF photometry on all the components (A = brightest QSO image, B = fainter QSO image, G\u00a0=\u00a0lens galaxy) for <em>g</em>-, <em>r</em>-, and <em>i</em>-bands. We use a Se\u0155sic profile with n\u00a0=\u00a04 (i.e. we assume a de Vaucouleurs profile) to fit the light distribution of the deflector and point-PSF to fit that of each QSO image. We fit all the components simultaneously. We include the results in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>, together with the spectroscopic redshift values for the sources and the photometric redshift values for the deflectors.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">To estimate the photometric redshifts of the deflectors we compared their PSF colours as derived above with galaxy spectra from the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS, DR14, Abolfathi et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>). In particular, for each deflector, we select all galaxies in <span class=\"monospace\">SpecPhotoAll</span> with colours within 3\u03c3 from the ones obtained from PSF photometry (we use the <span class=\"monospace\">psfMag</span> and its <span class=\"monospace\">psfMagErr</span> for each band) on the lens and retain their spectroscopic redshifts. Then, we fit a normal distribution to the resulting histograms (plotted in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>), obtaining the mean and standard deviation of the redshift that we adopted as the fiduciary photo-<em>z</em> and its uncertainty.</p>                        <a id=\"129345923\" scrollto-destination=\"129345923\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig4\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 4.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/483/3/10.1093_mnras_sty3407/1/m_sty3407fig4.jpeg?Expires=1611465313&amp;Signature=1DKjq7xmz8NPiYHvhfDjW5OljTkdM-zyctl~yIGFOFYUiVsgBs9IIzojvmwaXYqcQOD~lDtrnMeGujAK4kYloFKMSL45Dfk4hzPCuhoAjABSROzWNMgPWohS2DGUFJv3QWt68op3qieA0woOkodACUH3kj-LO863DLji5AIWZKiFzkSEhTBClUfD9wMu51XZymQ3fPpzoT0LqOBrw~V~~fNF-FrP5gX2HGxEu9Jg5kEMC5j1SExLQD1HLfGlXXOc1N~kVPAVQF78zylujeVSSz1Xv77IVjpqTPGkFWw2zu6IdD09FrbbOs8OI6elCExeS2B06pGPnCuqSjgPCgqbrA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Inference on the photometric redshifts of the deflectors in this sample, using spectroscopic redshifts from SDSS-DR14 SpecPhotoAll galaxies with similar PSF colours (within 3\u03c3 uncertainties). The number of galaxies plotted on the y-axis for each system has been normalized to the histogram maximum value.\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig4.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/129345923/sty3407fig4.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig4.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"129345923\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/483/3/10.1093_mnras_sty3407/1/sty3407fig4.jpeg?Expires=1611465313&Signature=CA17xb75dqBsOV2DsZ1dP1JrL3TMae6AqwaEwD7Ad9oKaoNwUki~9tjd4LGaEzNtPLTkwvJUeS6JWWIcii~mYXbIG4eEaUu~Bcx7LPmqwlGBY6d-xH-zKnONcG3X1N4-JB3lvElqijcyLKM5lpdt0LeTGq2UHTNd4zCQ7gskexuO6VEklJhyKU-wEXul4AIYhxrdWaZDiH5U-Jnrm8xiube5DLfQDspXDDpjqPITLeCmGYadso4uvWt88fmK4ZPRx8iO8qvKPQa~sOBJvA34U4G0nqsrkiebbH1THbpG5rJWPxd0GSxIdSIkJ6JggjKMQNXT7lYGlrpzTS~MVDaxNg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=129345923&ar=5251843&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig4.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Inference on the photometric redshifts of the deflectors in this sample, using spectroscopic redshifts from SDSS-DR14 <span class=\"monospace\">SpecPhotoAll</span> galaxies with similar PSF colours (within 3\u03c3 uncertainties). The number of galaxies plotted on the <em>y</em>-axis for each system has been normalized to the histogram maximum value.</p></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=129345924 id=\"129345924\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 LENS MODELS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We provide here lens model parameters for the confirmed systems. We adopt a Singular Isothermal Sphere with external shear (SIS\u00a0+\u00a0XS) described by an Einstein radius <em>R</em><sub>Ein</sub> and a shear amplitude \u03b3 and orientation. The models are fit to the relative astrometry of quasar images and deflectors from above. The errors are propagated from the shear direction and are proportional to1 \u00b1 \u03b3. The resulting Einstein radii are approximately half the image separations (within <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\approx }10{{\\ \\rm per\\ cent}}$|\u2060</span>), but the SIS\u00a0+\u00a0XS model allows us to account for degeneracies between monopole and quadrupole contributions to the mass. The resulting best-fitting parameters are given in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl3\" data-open=\"tbl3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>, where we also give the predicted magnitude differences and time delays. The main contribution of the time-delay uncertainties comes from the photometric redshift estimation. The model magnitude differences are in perfect agreement with the measured magnitude difference in <em>i</em>-band reported in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> for DES01xx-24xx, DES0247-6349, and KIDS2307-3039. For the remaining two systems, in one case the difference is underestimated by the model (DES03xx-44xx) and in the other case (DES2158-5812) it is overestimated by it. However, we note that multiple factors might affect the actual flux ratios of lensed quasars: the combination of time delays and source variability, microlensing, substructures, and differential dust reddening in the lens plane. Given that generally the B images show the most chromatic variation (redder than the brightest images), extinction probably plays a major role. Only deeper spectra and deeper photometry would enable quantitative studies of the objects (e.g. Yonehara et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1998</a>; Agnello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>).</p>                        <a id=\"129345926\" scrollto-destination=\"129345926\"></a>\r\n<div target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/129345926\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">Finally, we calculated the total projected mass within the Einstein radius, using the classical lens equation formula (see e.g. Schneider, Ehlers\u00a0&amp; Falco <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1992</a>) <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"update2011118_update2011118_equ2\" content-id=\"update2011118_update2011118_equ2\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray*}\r\nM_{\\mathrm{ Ein}} = R_{\\mathrm{ Ein}}^{2}\\dfrac{c^2D_{\\mathrm{ l}}D_{\\mathrm{ s}}}{4GD_{\\mathrm{ ls}}}, \r\n\\end{eqnarray*} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(2)</span></div>where <em>D</em><sub>l</sub> is the distance of the lens from the observer, <em>D</em><sub>s</sub> is the distance of the source from the observer, and <em>D</em><sub>ls</sub> is the relative distance between the lens and the source. We include the masses in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl3\" data-open=\"tbl3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>.</div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=129345928 id=\"129345928\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5>5 DISCUSSION AND FUTURE PROSPECTS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We have presented a sample of previously unknown lenses, found in the Southern hemisphere through new techniques relying on astrometric offsets, and spectroscopically confirmed. The success rate of 5/7 meets the expectations from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> and\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">S18</a>. The range of source redshifts and Einstein radii is consistent with <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">OM10</a> predictions, further suggesting that these searches are complete within the photometric completeness of <em>Gaia</em>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Compared to the depth of DES and KiDS, these objects are still at the bright end. This fact has been noted for various independent searches (see Treu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>, for forecasts on the DES); a large fraction of lenses with faint quasar sources is hitherto undiscovered, and different strategies of target and candidate selection are needed.<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn4\" data-open=\"fn4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">4</a></sup> This is shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a>, where the cumulative distributions of predicted candidate and confirmed lenses are shown. On the left-hand panel, we show the distribution of targets in DES (dashed line) calculated by the STRIDES Collaboration (Treu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) and the predictions from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">OM10</a> (dotted line). We compare these distributions with the ones of the <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> candidates, rescaled by 0.7 to account for the success rate of this campaign, finding a very good agreement. Moreover, we note that samples relying on optical selection through <em>Gaia</em>, such as the one presented in Treu et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>), saturate between <em>i</em> \u224818.5 and <em>i</em> \u224820.0 whereas samples including radio and X-ray preselection (such as <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>) extend to fainter magnitudes and follow the <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">OM10</a> predictions more closely. The last point appears even more clearly in the right-hand panel of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a> where we split the <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> candidates according to the preselection method. Below <em>i</em> \u224820.5 the number of lens candidates found through radio and X-rays is larger than the number of systems selected in the optical.</p>                        <a id=\"129345931\" scrollto-destination=\"129345931\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/483/3/10.1093_mnras_sty3407/1/m_sty3407fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611465313&amp;Signature=H5txsPy1G1HkD3usQXYXGIR43-o0dfyT9chE-CEENLNWN7j9IpFX1uMANpEkTB03Ubc58JSAQURxkIG~YOlEoHDj83c4sMeujjvgutaAwWdyB7M1fKiYHzez6pqJzZcft0TI2ZpptKNvzLH2uzX6EPR2PsRuxjzdeBUDJWZERNUF3qLB7bIrIyhwnymSpMZk5s2dukAbjKqheiZqzYLIwLsPLcBEflMJ3653UEx4Zk0dW1QZc6hRgJ~MWA13NIGF~wbSf3BU8NoLRdWXB~PRC6xuRAOJbwnPVIU3lf~rbM1z1f3AylhJE4TrlFUIwSgXOhbNy~g6JRUOwQX~4WEB~Q__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Left-hand panel: Cumulative number of targets in bins of i-band magnitudes from A18 (solid lines) and scaled for the 70\u00a0per\u2009cent successful rate obtained here. The comparison with the distribution of targets in DES (dashed line) calculated by the STRIDES Collaboration (Treu et\u00a0al. 2018) and with predictions from OM10 (dotted line) shows a very good agreement. Right-hand panel: Same as in the left-hand panels, but the different lines show candidates selected in A18 from optical bands versus candidates selected from other wavelengths. Selecting QSOs from radio or X-Ray allows us to find fainter lenses.\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig5.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/129345931/sty3407fig5.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig5.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"129345931\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/483/3/10.1093_mnras_sty3407/1/sty3407fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611465313&Signature=AZlVgvDYF-dkIzmIPJW8SBDTAbZLAqN4yHZfmfbUL7vFSY5BkU7QRLyhvUIOBpAF2Bp4NM8-oRY8xwT7zwKmIQhXDYZYxc2V9RGjIsqYdUZbzJhjqNiDP6wdVQiV8PsxTrQG3YwJax54NhtuVwA~HLtT3lyR94oRasnl6jTrqt1HF9YUOqCwqLXn7nGJ8pg7ft7zSpyyQZogwsXt8fhxOxqRgDEyFZ~JQd2hhU-e5D3biupEmxKl3FJrwdlFlKbqlNLL6ogpWIBLF4T5k0QSWLgZGcPThJFWVCYr0yrUGJ3p~0yDbiJjynKaNpNNrcmGcb8~f9nVwzgQK0uj93JPxg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=129345931&ar=5251843&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig5.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\"><em>Left-hand panel:</em> Cumulative number of targets in bins of <em>i</em>-band magnitudes from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> (solid lines) and scaled for the 70\u00a0per\u2009cent successful rate obtained here. The comparison with the distribution of targets in DES (dashed line) calculated by the STRIDES Collaboration (Treu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) and with predictions from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">OM10</a> (dotted line) shows a very good agreement. <em>Right-hand panel:</em> Same as in the left-hand panels, but the different lines show candidates selected in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> from optical bands versus candidates selected from other wavelengths. Selecting QSOs from radio or X-Ray allows us to find fainter lenses.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/483/3/10.1093_mnras_sty3407/1/m_sty3407fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611465313&amp;Signature=H5txsPy1G1HkD3usQXYXGIR43-o0dfyT9chE-CEENLNWN7j9IpFX1uMANpEkTB03Ubc58JSAQURxkIG~YOlEoHDj83c4sMeujjvgutaAwWdyB7M1fKiYHzez6pqJzZcft0TI2ZpptKNvzLH2uzX6EPR2PsRuxjzdeBUDJWZERNUF3qLB7bIrIyhwnymSpMZk5s2dukAbjKqheiZqzYLIwLsPLcBEflMJ3653UEx4Zk0dW1QZc6hRgJ~MWA13NIGF~wbSf3BU8NoLRdWXB~PRC6xuRAOJbwnPVIU3lf~rbM1z1f3AylhJE4TrlFUIwSgXOhbNy~g6JRUOwQX~4WEB~Q__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Left-hand panel: Cumulative number of targets in bins of i-band magnitudes from A18 (solid lines) and scaled for the 70\u00a0per\u2009cent successful rate obtained here. Right-hand panel: Same as in the left-hand panels, but the different lines show candidates selected in A18 from optical bands versus candidates selected from other wavelengths. Selecting QSOs from radio or X-Ray allows us to find fainter lenses.\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig5.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/129345931/sty3407fig5.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig5.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"129345931\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/483/3/10.1093_mnras_sty3407/1/sty3407fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611465313&Signature=AZlVgvDYF-dkIzmIPJW8SBDTAbZLAqN4yHZfmfbUL7vFSY5BkU7QRLyhvUIOBpAF2Bp4NM8-oRY8xwT7zwKmIQhXDYZYxc2V9RGjIsqYdUZbzJhjqNiDP6wdVQiV8PsxTrQG3YwJax54NhtuVwA~HLtT3lyR94oRasnl6jTrqt1HF9YUOqCwqLXn7nGJ8pg7ft7zSpyyQZogwsXt8fhxOxqRgDEyFZ~JQd2hhU-e5D3biupEmxKl3FJrwdlFlKbqlNLL6ogpWIBLF4T5k0QSWLgZGcPThJFWVCYr0yrUGJ3p~0yDbiJjynKaNpNNrcmGcb8~f9nVwzgQK0uj93JPxg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=129345931&ar=5251843&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig5.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\"><em>Left-hand panel:</em> Cumulative number of targets in bins of <em>i</em>-band magnitudes from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> (solid lines) and scaled for the 70\u00a0per\u2009cent successful rate obtained here. The comparison with the distribution of targets in DES (dashed line) calculated by the STRIDES Collaboration (Treu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) and with predictions from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">OM10</a> (dotted line) shows a very good agreement. <em>Right-hand panel:</em> Same as in the left-hand panels, but the different lines show candidates selected in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> from optical bands versus candidates selected from other wavelengths. Selecting QSOs from radio or X-Ray allows us to find fainter lenses.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The brightness of most confirmed lenses also means that spectroscopic follow-up, to measure the kinematics of the deflectors, is affordable with current-generation facilities. Through monitoring with nightly-cadence, an accuracy of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5{{\\ \\rm per\\ cent}}$|</span> should be attainable on the time delay (\u0394<em>t</em>) between quasar light curves in systems with \u0394<em>t</em> \u2273 25\u00a0d (Courbin, private communication). Moreover, if the deflector\u2019s velocity dispersion \u03c3 is measured, the combination <em>c</em><sup>3</sup>\u0394<em>t</em>/\u03c3<sup>2</sup>\u00a0\u221d\u00a0<em>D</em><sub>l</sub> of time delay and kinematics would make these systems standard rulers at <em><em>z</em></em>\u00a0= 0.2\u22120.65, to within <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\approx }20{{\\ \\rm per\\ cent}}$|</span> uncertainties (Jee, Komatsu\u00a0&amp; Suyu <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Shajib, Treu\u00a0&amp; Agnello <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>). For lenses with lower deflector redshift, the time-delay distance <em>D</em><sub>\u0394<em>t</em></sub>\u00a0= <em>D</em><sub>l</sub><em>D</em><sub>s</sub>/((1 + <em>z</em><sub>l</sub>)<em>D</em><sub>ls</sub>) is proportional to <em>D</em><sub>l</sub> with a factor that is only weakly dependent on cosmological parameters (\u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>, \u03a9<sub>m</sub>). Securing spectroscopic redshifts of the deflectors and measuring time delays would then yield two angular diameter distances per lens.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=129345933 id=\"129345933\" class=\"backacknowledgements-title\" >ACKNOWLEDGEMENTS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The authors wish to thank the anonymous referee for interesting and constructive comments that helped in improving the quality and clarity of the paper.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">CS and NRN have received funding from the European Union\u2019s Horizon 2020 research and innovation programme under the Marie Sklodowska-Curie actions grant agreement No 664931 and No 721463 to the SUNDIAL ITN network, respectively. CT acknowledges funding from the INAF PRIN-SKA 2017 program No 1.05.01.88.04.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=129345936 id=\"129345936\" class=\"backfootnotegroup-title\" class=\"article-content-filter js-article-content-filter\" data-content-filter=\"supplementary-data\">\r\n                                    <a href=\"javascript:;\"><span>Supplementary Data</span></a>\r\n                                </li>\r\n                            </ul>\r\n                        </li>\r\n                        <li class=\"toolbar-item\">\r\n    <div <div class=\"widget widget-ArticleFulltext widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=129345898 id=\"129345898\" class=\"abstract-title\" >ABSTRACT</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Gravitationally lensed quasars are valuable, but extremely rare, probes of observational cosmology and extragalactic astrophysics. Progress in these fields has been limited just by the paucity of systems with good ancillary data. Here we present a first spectroscopic confirmation of lenses discovered in the Southern Sky from the DES and KiDS-DR3 footprints. We have targeted seven high-graded candidates, selected with new techniques, with NTT-EFOSC2, and confirmed five of them. We provide source spectroscopic redshifts, image separations, <em>gri</em> photometry, and first lens model parameters. The success rate of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\sim } 70{{\\ \\rm per\\ cent}}$|</span> confirms our forecasts, based on the comparison between the number of candidate doubles and quadruplets in our searches over a \u22485000\u00a0deg<sup>2</sup> footprint and theoretical predictions.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"surveys\">surveys</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;Galaxies: formation&quot;\">Galaxies: formation</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=129345900 id=\"129345900\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">When a quasar (QSO) is strongly lensed by a galaxy, it results in multiple images of the same source, possibly accompanied by arcs or rings that map the lensed host galaxy. The light curves of different images are offset by a measurable time delay that depends on cosmological distances to lens and source and the gravitational potential of the lens (Refsdal <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1964</a>), which in turn enables one-step measurements of the expansion history of the Universe and the dark-matter haloes of massive lens galaxies at up to <em>z</em> \u223c 0.5 (e.g. Suyu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). The microlensing effect on the multiple QSO images, induced by stars in the deflector, provides a quantitative handle on the stellar content of the lens galaxies (e.g. Schechter\u00a0&amp; Wambsganss <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Bate et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Oguri, Rusu\u00a0&amp; Falco <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>) and, simultaneously, can constrain the inner structure of the source quasar, both accretion disc size and thermal profile (e.g. Anguita et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Eigenbrod et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Motta et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) as well as the geometry of the broad-line region (e.g. Sluse et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Guerras et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Braibant et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). Finally, source reconstruction of the lensed QSO and its host give a direct view of QSO-host co-evolution up to <em>z</em> \u223c 2 (e.g. Peng et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Ding et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). However, lensed quasars are rare on the sky: typically \u223c0.1 per deg<sup>2</sup> at depth and resolution of present-day surveys (Oguri\u00a0&amp; Marshall <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>, hereafter <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">OM10</a>), since they require a very close alignment of quasars with foreground massive galaxies, or galaxy clusters. The advent of various wide-field surveys, charting extended areas in both hemispheres, helps to overcome the intrinsic rarity of lensed quasars, provided that suitable techniques are devised in order to mine them in massive data bases.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Within our team, we have developed multiple techniques of data mining for lensed quasar searches and recently applied them with success to the Kilo Degree Survey and to the Dark Energy Survey (Agnello\u00a0&amp; Spiniello <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a> and Spiniello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>, hereafter <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> and\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">S18</a>, respectively). We combined different methods to pre-select QSOs, tested their performance and complementarity, and published a list of high-grade candidates, to facilitate (possibly independent) spectroscopic follow-up campaigns.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Here, we present results from the first of these follow-up campaigns, based on data acquired with EFOSC2 (the ESO Faint Object Spectrograph and Camera) mounted at the Nasmyth B focus of the 3.6\u00a0m New Technology Telescope (NTT). We give details of the selected candidates in the next section (Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a>). We report on the spectroscopic run in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a> and provide photometry and lens model results in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>. We finally conclude in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>. Whenever needed, we adopt a flat lambda cold dark matter cosmology with \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>\u00a0= 0.7 and <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0= 70\u2009km\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup>\u00a0Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>. Magnitudes from DES and KiDS are in the AB system while the ones from WISE are in the Vega system.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=129345904 id=\"129345904\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 CANDIDATE SELECTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We selected our candidates from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">S18</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>, and from a more recent (hitherto unpublished) list of high-grade candidates found in a similar way. We refer to the two mentioned papers for a detailed description of the morphology- and photometry-based methods that we developed to find lens candidates in wide-sky photometric multiband surveys. The new DES candidates were selected using astrometric offsets of WISE-preselected objects (with the same WISE cuts as in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>) between DES and <em>Gaia</em> J2000 coordinates, whereas in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> we were considering offsets between 2MASS and <em>Gaia</em> coordinates. The reason behind this method can be explained by noting that if the deflector and quasar images contribute differently in different bands or in data with different image quality, this should result in centroid offsets of the same object among different surveys. We followed the same procedure as in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> to detrend such astrometric offsets, and targets were required to have field-corrected offsets between 0.27 and 2.0\u00a0arcsec (following tests by <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">S18</a> and\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Targets were then visually inspected via the NCSA-DES access cut-out server<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn1\" data-open=\"fn1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">1</a></sup> to assemble a final list of candidates. Some high-grade candidates were lost at visual inspection, due to visualization issues from large queries in the NCSA web interface (we expected this since <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>). As per STRIDES<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn2\" data-open=\"fn2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">2</a></sup> internal agreements, the full list of lens candidates from DES-versus-<em>Gaia</em> offsets will not be disclosed yet.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Some of our candidates have also been found by another group at the same time (Lemon et\u00a0al. in preparation). Following publication agreements within STRIDES, we give here partially blinded coordinates for two of them. Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> reports coordinates and infrared magnitudes (used in the stage of pre-selection) of the systems.</p>                        <a id=\"129345908\" scrollto-destination=\"129345908\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl1\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table 1.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">List of observed candidates with the infrared magnitudes from the WISE catalogue (Wright et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) that have been used at the pre-selection stage (for some systems, errors of magnitudes are missing from the WISE catalogue). Lenses with partly blinded coordinates have been found independently also by Lemon et al (in preparation), here indicated as L18.</p></div> </div><div class=\"table-overflow\"><table><thead><tr><th>ID<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>RA (J2000)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>Dec. (J2000)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>W1 (mag)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>W2 paper, and L18\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/129345908\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">For all the candidates, we perform Direct Image Analysis (DIA), as detailed in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">S18</a>. Briefly, a PSF model is fit and subsequently subtracted from the survey image to check for the presence of signal from the deflector. In particular, using the <span class=\"small-caps\">pyraf</span> package<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn3\" data-open=\"fn3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">3</a></sup> on the <em>r</em>-band images, we simultaneously fit a point-PSF model to the QSO multiple images. We then generated subtracted images which we visually inspect to identify the position of the deflector. For the DES systems, DIA was performed after the spectroscopic run, since we did not use it in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We show the <em>gri</em> cut-outs (left-hand panel) and the DIA residuals (right-hand panels) for the candidates reported in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> candidates presented in this paper.</p></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=129345913 id=\"129345913\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 SPECTROSCOPIC FOLLOW-UP</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Three nights on NTT-EFOSC2 (P0101.A-0298, PI: Anguita) were allocated for follow-up in 2018 July. However, the run was mostly weathered out and we could observe only seven candidates, each with 20 min of integration time. The seeing was stable at 1.0 \u00b1 0.2\u00a0arcsec, spectra were reduced using standard (ESO-released) pipelines, and the quasar traces were optimally de-blended using a superpostion of Gaussian profiles in the spatial direction (see Morgan et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>; Agnello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We have confirmed five out of seven lenses, selected from wide-sky photometric surveys, namely DES and KiDS, in the Southern Sky. Concerning the two remaining candidates, KIDS2300-3104 resulted to be a couple of stars, while for bf DES2105-4249 only one trace showed emission lines in its spectrum. This system is therefore not a lensed quasar where the two point-like sources are multiple images of the same object. It is most likely a projection effect of a galaxy\u00a0+\u00a0QSOs.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This success rate of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\sim }70{{\\ \\rm per\\ cent}}$|</span> is slightly higher but still consistent with the estimates from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>, considering the number of high-graded candidates versus the number of expected lenses over the DES footprint (adopting the lensing rates by <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">OM10</a>).</p><div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">The NTT spectra of the five confirmed lensed QSOs are shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>, where we also highlight some of the stronger emission lines that enabled the determination of source redshifts, such as CIV\u00a0\u03bb1549, L\u03b1, or Mg\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>\u00a0\u03bb2799. The redshifts were determined with a simultaneous Gaussian fitting to the main emission lines on the spectra of the single components of the quasars, after subtracting the continuum with a fourth-order polynomial function. We note that, although some features deviate from a Gaussian profile, this assumption is sufficient to correctly fit the peak of the lines and measure the redshift of their central wavelength. Once identified the <em>i</em>-th emission lines and their rest-frame wavelength (<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">\u2060|$\\lambda _{0, \\rm i}$|\u2060</span>), we defined the peaks of the Gaussians as <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\lambda _{0, \\rm i}(1+z)$|\u2060</span>, hence <em><em>z</em></em> is a common free parameter for the fitting function, defined as <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"update2011118_update2011118_equ1\" content-id=\"update2011118_update2011118_equ1\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray*}\r\n\\Sigma _{i} A_i \\mathrm{ e}^\\frac{[(\\lambda -\\lambda _{0, \\rm i})(1+z)]^2}{2\\sigma _i^2}, \r\n\\end{eqnarray*} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(1)</span></div>where <em>A<sub>i</sub></em> are normalization factors which account for the peak high, and \u03c3<sub><em>i</em></sub> measure the width of the line. In order to assess the statistical error on the redshift estimates, we have resampled 100\u00a0times the spectrum of every source in the fitted range including the three brightest emission-line features. We have randomly re-extracted each pixel value around the current one assuming Gaussian noise given by the rms of the continuum in the regions close to the fitting window. We have then obtained the mean and standard deviation of the best-fitting redshift obtained using a Levenberg\u2013Marquardt method for \u03c7<sup>2</sup> minimization over the 100 resampled spectra. These are reported in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> for all confirmed quasars as final redshift estimates with their statistical uncertainty.</div>                        <a id=\"129345918\" scrollto-destination=\"129345918\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/483/3/10.1093_mnras_sty3407/1/m_sty3407fig3.jpeg?Expires=1611465313&amp;Signature=mVQC07LIPVHGiFvOXfKsEVoHBHI9xWRjzvb9ALyHETgSKqKGhSYs5R3Sm9xNCZa1gxrZrc9qIlF26pF4psZfj1TG6oXy-4XcACYGtba3ykykFiOzn7-qn4U~IbrIhVW0qsmkjN4RSb4aMd-6Uow-gz1ZNF5jnRpKrKZEFnbR1HiwkkzzMZWMaxjVn1oDU9PKAYit6AgjMLCCmFWf3JTCuCjOkxp~XmwOV2ENi-E1GKcTvKz8N2Fmd92afQkWA~5fr98e-Ayy-HRLQFbJC2hl6j2zqqMWRAfPWhKfj6GAr3xIjq~eZ4-brCN0l8xJ4Y2GDuxVkEe7xyM0~PMbM~X15g__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"1D extracted spectra of the two quasar images for the five confirmed new lenses. The most prominent emission lines which allowed us to infer the redshift of the sources are highlighted in the plots. Component A (brighter) is always plotted in the upper panels, while component B (fainter) in the lower ones. The wavelength is always plotted in the observed frame.\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig3.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/129345918/sty3407fig3.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig3.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"129345918\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/483/3/10.1093_mnras_sty3407/1/sty3407fig3.jpeg?Expires=1611465313&Signature=juyoOOPc-4JdY0sUKI-x6lefjBq51N91MIZyB4PN2Yl-fBICAN7uoB4Gs6WqxY~TgehCgWv7sPGSQmdIgs2E9UzTk~KJIXjh0GDurdoo2oGBlc50y1r41A1j0Om8V9TNupWJl53isw4NEpXh72nnzyRgRSmNCBjXzIxOUjxMSIy4hHM~FeHUTQYc6dzsKV4rVRYIZLCYKVZBzTI1-VQLipYq7NYD5bRj0RB22e3Q1OCx3xIcyGMBi38S-IBRQ1b5c3YHtvkxfDO0V0L-TNGBd5zDr3nhAqEhX1Ib3uSYWFmFvOacxGkQ8vCeavtWQFYzOvas2nb9dEbdwBfl8jvDpw__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=129345918&ar=5251843&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig3.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">1D extracted spectra of the two quasar images for the five confirmed new lenses. The most prominent emission lines which allowed us to infer the redshift of the sources are highlighted in the plots. Component A (brighter) is always plotted in the upper panels, while component B (fainter) in the lower ones. The wavelength is always plotted in the observed frame.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/483/3/10.1093_mnras_sty3407/1/m_sty3407fig3.jpeg?Expires=1611465313&amp;Signature=mVQC07LIPVHGiFvOXfKsEVoHBHI9xWRjzvb9ALyHETgSKqKGhSYs5R3Sm9xNCZa1gxrZrc9qIlF26pF4psZfj1TG6oXy-4XcACYGtba3ykykFiOzn7-qn4U~IbrIhVW0qsmkjN4RSb4aMd-6Uow-gz1ZNF5jnRpKrKZEFnbR1HiwkkzzMZWMaxjVn1oDU9PKAYit6AgjMLCCmFWf3JTCuCjOkxp~XmwOV2ENi-E1GKcTvKz8N2Fmd92afQkWA~5fr98e-Ayy-HRLQFbJC2hl6j2zqqMWRAfPWhKfj6GAr3xIjq~eZ4-brCN0l8xJ4Y2GDuxVkEe7xyM0~PMbM~X15g__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"1D extracted spectra of the two quasar images for the five confirmed new lenses. class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/129345919\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Unfortunately, the faint traces of the lensing galaxies in the spectra did not allow us to securely identify deflector redshifts using the same method. We then estimate photometric redshift distributions using deflector magnitudes from the DES and KIDS multiband images, as explained below.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Using <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> (Peng et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>) we performed PSF photometry on all the components (A = brightest QSO image, B = fainter QSO image, G\u00a0=\u00a0lens galaxy) for <em>g</em>-, <em>r</em>-, and <em>i</em>-bands. We use a Se\u0155sic profile with n\u00a0=\u00a04 (i.e. we assume a de Vaucouleurs profile) to fit the light distribution of the deflector and point-PSF to fit that of each QSO image. We fit all the components simultaneously. We include the results in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>, together with the spectroscopic redshift values for the sources and the photometric redshift values for the deflectors.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">To estimate the photometric redshifts of the deflectors we compared their PSF colours as derived above with galaxy spectra from the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS, DR14, Abolfathi et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>). In particular, for each deflector, we select all galaxies in <span class=\"monospace\">SpecPhotoAll</span> with colours within 3\u03c3 from the ones obtained from PSF photometry (we use the <span class=\"monospace\">psfMag</span> and its <span class=\"monospace\">psfMagErr</span> for each band) on the lens and retain their spectroscopic redshifts. Then, we fit a normal distribution to the resulting histograms (plotted in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>), obtaining the mean and standard deviation of the redshift that we adopted as the fiduciary photo-<em>z</em> and its uncertainty.</p>                        <a id=\"129345923\" scrollto-destination=\"129345923\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig4\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 4.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/483/3/10.1093_mnras_sty3407/1/m_sty3407fig4.jpeg?Expires=1611465313&amp;Signature=1DKjq7xmz8NPiYHvhfDjW5OljTkdM-zyctl~yIGFOFYUiVsgBs9IIzojvmwaXYqcQOD~lDtrnMeGujAK4kYloFKMSL45Dfk4hzPCuhoAjABSROzWNMgPWohS2DGUFJv3QWt68op3qieA0woOkodACUH3kj-LO863DLji5AIWZKiFzkSEhTBClUfD9wMu51XZymQ3fPpzoT0LqOBrw~V~~fNF-FrP5gX2HGxEu9Jg5kEMC5j1SExLQD1HLfGlXXOc1N~kVPAVQF78zylujeVSSz1Xv77IVjpqTPGkFWw2zu6IdD09FrbbOs8OI6elCExeS2B06pGPnCuqSjgPCgqbrA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Inference on the photometric redshifts of the deflectors in this sample, using spectroscopic redshifts from SDSS-DR14 SpecPhotoAll galaxies with similar PSF colours (within 3\u03c3 uncertainties). The number of galaxies plotted on the <em>y</em>-axis for each system has been normalized to the histogram maximum value.</p></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=129345924 id=\"129345924\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 LENS MODELS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We provide here lens model parameters for the confirmed systems. We adopt a Singular Isothermal Sphere with external shear (SIS\u00a0+\u00a0XS) described by an Einstein radius <em>R</em><sub>Ein</sub> and a shear amplitude \u03b3 and orientation. The models are fit to the relative astrometry of quasar images and deflectors from above. The errors are propagated from the shear direction and are proportional to1 \u00b1 \u03b3. The resulting Einstein radii are approximately half the image separations (within <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\approx }10{{\\ \\rm per\\ cent}}$|\u2060</span>), but the SIS\u00a0+\u00a0XS model allows us to account for degeneracies between monopole and quadrupole contributions to the mass. The resulting best-fitting parameters are given in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl3\" data-open=\"tbl3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>, where we also give the predicted magnitude differences and time delays. The main contribution of the time-delay uncertainties comes from the photometric redshift estimation. The model magnitude differences are in perfect agreement with the measured magnitude difference in <em>i</em>-band reported in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> for DES01xx-24xx, DES0247-6349, and KIDS2307-3039. For the remaining two systems, in one case the difference is underestimated by the model (DES03xx-44xx) and in the other case (DES2158-5812) it is overestimated by it. However, we note that multiple factors might affect the actual flux ratios of lensed quasars: the combination of time delays and source variability, microlensing, substructures, and differential dust reddening in the lens plane. Given that generally the B images show the most chromatic variation (redder than the brightest images), extinction probably plays a major role. Only deeper spectra and deeper photometry would enable quantitative studies of the objects (e.g. Yonehara et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1998</a>; Agnello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>).</p>                        <a id=\"129345926\" scrollto-destination=\"129345926\"></a>\r\n<div
