class=\"table-wrap-foot\"><span id=\"fn-tblf26\"></span><div content-id=\"tblf26\"><span class=\"fn\"><p class=\"chapter-para\"><em>Notes</em>: <em>a</em>: model magnitude difference between A and B images</p></span></div><span id=\"fn-tblf27\"></span><div content-id=\"tblf27\"><span class=\"fn\"><p class=\"chapter-para\"><em>b</em>: the errors are propagated from the shear direction uncertainties and are proportional to 1 \u00b1 \u03b3</p></span></div></div><div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/129345926\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">Finally, we calculated the total projected mass within the Einstein radius, using the classical lens equation formula (see e.g. Schneider, Ehlers\u00a0&amp; Falco <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1992</a>) <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"update2011118_update2011118_equ2\" content-id=\"update2011118_update2011118_equ2\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray*}\r\nM_{\\mathrm{ Ein}} = R_{\\mathrm{ Ein}}^{2}\\dfrac{c^2D_{\\mathrm{ l}}D_{\\mathrm{ s}}}{4GD_{\\mathrm{ ls}}}, \r\n\\end{eqnarray*} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(2)</span></div>where <em>D</em><sub>l</sub> is the distance of the lens from the observer, <em>D</em><sub>s</sub> is the distance of the source from the observer, and <em>D</em><sub>ls</sub> is the relative distance between the lens and the source. We include the masses in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl3\" data-open=\"tbl3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>.</div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=129345928 id=\"129345928\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5>5 DISCUSSION AND FUTURE PROSPECTS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We have presented a sample of previously unknown lenses, found in the Southern hemisphere through new techniques relying on astrometric offsets, and spectroscopically confirmed. The success rate of 5/7 meets the expectations from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> and\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">S18</a>. The range of source redshifts and Einstein radii is consistent with <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">OM10</a> predictions, further suggesting that these searches are complete within the photometric completeness of <em>Gaia</em>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Compared to the depth of DES and KiDS, these objects are still at the bright end. This fact has been noted for various independent searches (see Treu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>, for forecasts on the DES); a large fraction of lenses with faint quasar sources is hitherto undiscovered, and different strategies of target and candidate selection are needed.<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn4\" data-open=\"fn4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">4</a></sup> This is shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a>, where the cumulative distributions of predicted candidate and confirmed lenses are shown. On the left-hand panel, we show the distribution of targets in DES (dashed line) calculated by the STRIDES Collaboration (Treu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) and the predictions from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">OM10</a> (dotted line). We compare these distributions with the ones of the <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> candidates, rescaled by 0.7 to account for the success rate of this campaign, finding a very good agreement. Moreover, we note that samples relying on optical selection through <em>Gaia</em>, such as the one presented in Treu et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>), saturate between <em>i</em> \u224818.5 and <em>i</em> \u224820.0 whereas samples including radio and X-ray preselection (such as <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>) extend to fainter magnitudes and follow the <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">OM10</a> predictions more closely. The last point appears even more clearly in the right-hand panel of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a> where we split the <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> candidates according to the preselection method. Below <em>i</em> \u224820.5 the number of lens candidates found through radio and X-rays is larger than the number of systems selected in the optical.</p>                        <a id=\"129345931\" scrollto-destination=\"129345931\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/483/3/10.1093_mnras_sty3407/1/m_sty3407fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611465313&amp;Signature=H5txsPy1G1HkD3usQXYXGIR43-o0dfyT9chE-CEENLNWN7j9IpFX1uMANpEkTB03Ubc58JSAQURxkIG~YOlEoHDj83c4sMeujjvgutaAwWdyB7M1fKiYHzez6pqJzZcft0TI2ZpptKNvzLH2uzX6EPR2PsRuxjzdeBUDJWZERNUF3qLB7bIrIyhwnymSpMZk5s2dukAbjKqheiZqzYLIwLsPLcBEflMJ3653UEx4Zk0dW1QZc6hRgJ~MWA13NIGF~wbSf3BU8NoLRdWXB~PRC6xuRAOJbwnPVIU3lf~rbM1z1f3AylhJE4TrlFUIwSgXOhbNy~g6JRUOwQX~4WEB~Q__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Left-hand panel: Cumulative number of targets in bins of i-band magnitudes from A18 (solid lines) and scaled for the 70\u00a0per\u2009cent successful rate obtained here. Selecting QSOs from radio or X-Ray allows us to find fainter lenses.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/483/3/10.1093_mnras_sty3407/1/m_sty3407fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611465313&amp;Signature=H5txsPy1G1HkD3usQXYXGIR43-o0dfyT9chE-CEENLNWN7j9IpFX1uMANpEkTB03Ubc58JSAQURxkIG~YOlEoHDj83c4sMeujjvgutaAwWdyB7M1fKiYHzez6pqJzZcft0TI2ZpptKNvzLH2uzX6EPR2PsRuxjzdeBUDJWZERNUF3qLB7bIrIyhwnymSpMZk5s2dukAbjKqheiZqzYLIwLsPLcBEflMJ3653UEx4Zk0dW1QZc6hRgJ~MWA13NIGF~wbSf3BU8NoLRdWXB~PRC6xuRAOJbwnPVIU3lf~rbM1z1f3AylhJE4TrlFUIwSgXOhbNy~g6JRUOwQX~4WEB~Q__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Left-hand panel: Cumulative number of targets in bins of i-band magnitudes from A18 (solid lines) and scaled for the 70\u00a0per\u2009cent successful rate obtained here. The comparison with the distribution of targets in DES (dashed line) calculated by the STRIDES Collaboration (Treu et\u00a0al. 2018) and with predictions from OM10 (dotted line) shows a very good agreement. Right-hand panel: Same as in the left-hand panels, but the different lines show candidates selected in A18 from optical bands versus candidates selected from other wavelengths. Selecting QSOs from radio or X-Ray allows us to find fainter lenses.\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig5.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/129345931/sty3407fig5.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig5.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"129345931\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/483/3/10.1093_mnras_sty3407/1/sty3407fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611465313&Signature=AZlVgvDYF-dkIzmIPJW8SBDTAbZLAqN4yHZfmfbUL7vFSY5BkU7QRLyhvUIOBpAF2Bp4NM8-oRY8xwT7zwKmIQhXDYZYxc2V9RGjIsqYdUZbzJhjqNiDP6wdVQiV8PsxTrQG3YwJax54NhtuVwA~HLtT3lyR94oRasnl6jTrqt1HF9YUOqCwqLXn7nGJ8pg7ft7zSpyyQZogwsXt8fhxOxqRgDEyFZ~JQd2hhU-e5D3biupEmxKl3FJrwdlFlKbqlNLL6ogpWIBLF4T5k0QSWLgZGcPThJFWVCYr0yrUGJ3p~0yDbiJjynKaNpNNrcmGcb8~f9nVwzgQK0uj93JPxg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=129345931&ar=5251843&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty3407fig5.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\"><em>Left-hand panel:</em> Cumulative number of targets in bins of <em>i</em>-band magnitudes from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> (solid lines) and scaled for the 70\u00a0per\u2009cent successful rate obtained here. The comparison with the distribution of targets in DES (dashed line) calculated by the STRIDES Collaboration (Treu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) and with predictions from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">OM10</a> (dotted line) shows a very good agreement. <em>Right-hand panel:</em> Same as in the left-hand panels, but the different lines show candidates selected in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a> from optical bands versus candidates selected from other wavelengths. Selecting QSOs from radio or X-Ray allows us to find fainter lenses.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The brightness of most confirmed lenses also means that spectroscopic follow-up, to measure the kinematics of the deflectors, is affordable with current-generation facilities. Through monitoring with nightly-cadence, an accuracy of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5{{\\ \\rm per\\ cent}}$|</span> should be attainable on the time delay (\u0394<em>t</em>) between quasar light curves in systems with \u0394<em>t</em> \u2273 25\u00a0d (Courbin, private communication). Moreover, if the deflector\u2019s velocity dispersion \u03c3 is measured, the combination <em>c</em><sup>3</sup>\u0394<em>t</em>/\u03c3<sup>2</sup>\u00a0\u221d\u00a0<em>D</em><sub>l</sub> of time delay and kinematics would make these systems standard rulers at <em><em>z</em></em>\u00a0= 0.2\u22120.65, to within <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\approx }20{{\\ \\rm per\\ cent}}$|</span> uncertainties (Jee, Komatsu\u00a0&amp; Suyu <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Shajib, Treu\u00a0&amp; Agnello <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>). For lenses with lower deflector redshift, the time-delay distance <em>D</em><sub>\u0394<em>t</em></sub>\u00a0= <em>D</em><sub>l</sub><em>D</em><sub>s</sub>/((1 + <em>z</em><sub>l</sub>)<em>D</em><sub>ls</sub>) is proportional to <em>D</em><sub>l</sub> with a factor that is only weakly dependent on cosmological parameters (\u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>, \u03a9<sub>m</sub>). Securing spectroscopic redshifts of the deflectors and measuring time delays would then yield two angular diameter distances per lens.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=129345933 id=\"129345933\" class=\"backacknowledgements-title\" >ACKNOWLEDGEMENTS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The authors wish to thank the anonymous referee for interesting and constructive comments that helped in improving the quality and clarity of the paper.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">CS and NRN have received funding from the European Union\u2019s Horizon 2020 research and innovation programme under the Marie Sklodowska-Curie actions grant agreement No 664931 and No 721463 to the SUNDIAL ITN network, respectively. Moreover, we note that samples relying on optical selection through <em>Gaia</em>, such as the one presented in Treu et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>), saturate between <em>i</em> \u224818.5 and <em>i</em> \u224820.0 whereas samples including radio and X-ray preselection (such as <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">A18</a>) extend to fainter magnitudes and follow the <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">OM10</a> predictions more closely. China), AG(INAF - Osservatorio Astrofisico di Arcetri, Largo Enrico Fermi 5, I-50125 Firenze, Italy)"], "journal_name": "Monthly Notices of the Royal Astronomical Society", "volume": "483", "publication_year": "2019/03/1", "start_page": "3888", "end_page": "3893", "keywords": ["gravitational lensing: strong", "surveys", "Galaxies: formation", "Astrophysics - Astrophysics of Galaxies"], "url": "https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2019MNRAS.483.3888S", "abstract": "Gravitationally lensed quasars are valuable, but extremely rare, probes of observational cosmology and extragalactic astrophysics. Progress in these fields has been limited just by the paucity of systems with good ancillary data. Here we present a first spectroscopic confirmation of lenses discovered in the Southern Sky from the DES and KiDS-DR3 footprints. We have targeted seven high-graded candidates, selected with new techniques, with NTT-EFOSC2, and confirmed five of them. We provide source spectroscopic redshifts, image separations, gri photometry, and first lens model parameters. The success rate of {\u223c } 70{{ per cent}} confirms our forecasts, based on the comparison between the number of candidate doubles and quadruplets in our searches over a \u22485000 deg<SUP>2</SUP> footprint and theoretical predictions.", "doi": "10.1093/mnras/sty3407", "custom1": "eprint: arXiv:1811.01053", "issn": "0035-8711", "number": "3"}, "Inspection status": "Incomplete"}
